## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a population (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size. Classical ecological models describe growth rates through various density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (growth rate with logarithmic density dependence)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (P + c2) (cubic growth rate with two critical densities)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth generalization)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic environmental forcing on growth)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (compensatory density dependence)
- Quadratic-cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density dependence expansion)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing environment)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P → density-independent (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c*P
- Quadratic term P² with negative coefficient → density-dependent self-limitation / intraspecific competition
- Cubic term P³ or product P*(P-a)*(K-P) → Allee effect with critical population thresholds
- Logarithmic dependence log(P) → Gompertz-type growth, asymmetric sigmoidal trajectory
- Rational form P/(1+c*P) → compensatory density dependence with smooth saturation
- Fractional power P^c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-limited growth (e.g., nutrient absorption scaling)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Exponential time factor exp(c*t) → non-stationary environment with trending resource availability
- Sign change in dP_dt at specific P values → equilibrium points / carrying capacity identification
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria in population dynamics
